Refuting the Doctrine of Obligation upon God
Refutes the Mu'tazilite claim that God must do what is best.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Sunni tradition rejects the Mu'tazilite claim that God must do what is best for His creation, and how the Quran affirms God's absolute freedom and choice.

Core Idea
God’s actions are not bound by external obligations; they are expressions of His will and wisdom.

The Mu'tazilites argued that God is obligated to do what is most beneficial for His creatures. The Sunni reply, as presented here, exposes the logical and scriptural flaws in this claim. This passage shows how the Sunni position preserves God's sovereignty while affirming His wisdom and justice.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Mu'tazilite claim
Recognize that they claim al-aṣlaḥ (the most beneficial) is obligatory upon God.
2
Follow the first refutation: the argument from suffering
Notice how the existence of suffering disproves the claim.
The passage gives the example of the disbelieving poor person who suffers in both worlds.
3
Follow the second refutation: the argument from choice
See how tafḍīl (preferential treatment) would be impossible if the best were obligatory.
4
Examine the Quranic proof
Read the verses from al-Qaṣaṣ and al-Baqarah that affirm God's absolute will and choice.
These verses directly contradict the Mu'tazilite position.
5
Learn the Sunni position
Understand that nothing is obligatory upon God; His actions are permissible and either beneficence or justice.
Reason does not impose obligations on God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نقضُ أهل السنَّةِ لمسألة الإيجاب على الله تعالى
خبر المبتدأ ، أي : مُزَيَّنُ الظَّاهر (۱) فاسد الباطن فهو باطل ؛ لأنَّه لو وجب عليه تعالى الأصلح لعباده لما خلق الكافر الفقير المُعذِّبَ في الدُّنيا بالفقر وفي الآخرة بالعذاب الأليم المُخلَّد ، لا سيّما المُبتلى في الدُّنيا بالأسقام والمحن والآفات ، وأيضا لو وجب عليه الأصلحُ لما بقي للتفضيل مجالٌ (۲) ، ولم يكن تعالى خِيرَةً في الإنعام ، وهو باطل ؛ لقوله تعالى : ﴿وَرَبُّكَ يَخْلُقُ مَا يَشَاءُ وَيَختَارُ [القصص: ٦٨] . ويَخْتَصُّ بِرَحْمَتِهِ مَن يَشَاءُ ﴾ [البقرة: ١٠٥] .
[ نقضُ أهل السنّةِ لمسألة الإيجاب على الله تعالى]
(ما) أي: ليس (عَلَيْهِ) تعالى لخَلْقِه شيءٌ (وَاجِبُ) مِن فعل أو ترك ؛ لأنَّ أفعاله كلَّها جائزة بالنظر إلى ذاتها (۳) ، واقعةٌ على وجه الإحسان والفضل، أو على وجه المُؤاخذة والعدل، لا يجب منها شيءٌ عقلا ولا يستحيل (4) .
Refutation of the people of the Sunnah concerning the issue of obligation upon Allah Almighty. The predicate of the subject, i.e., externally adorned (1) but internally corrupt, so it is false. Because if the most beneficial (al-aṣlaḥ) were obligatory upon Him Almighty for His servants, He would not have created the disbelieving poor person who is punished in this world with poverty and in the Hereafter with eternal painful torment, especially one afflicted in this world with illnesses, hardships, and calamities. Also, if the most beneficial were obligatory upon Him, there would be no room for preference (tafḍīl) (2), and He Almighty would not have choice (khīrah) in bestowing favors, and this is false because of His saying, the Exalted: 'And your Lord creates what He wills and chooses' [al-Qaṣaṣ: 68], and 'He specifies His mercy to whom He wills' [al-Baqarah: 105]. [Refutation of the people of the Sunnah concerning the issue of obligation upon Allah Almighty] (What) i.e., there is not (upon Him) Almighty for His creation anything (obligatory) of action or abandonment, because all His actions are permissible (jā'izah) with respect to their essence (3), occurring in the manner of beneficence and generosity, or in the manner of taking to account and justice; nothing thereof is obligatory by reason (ʿaqlan) nor impossible (4).
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazilite doctrine that God is obligated to do what is best (al-aṣlaḥ) for His creation. The author begins by stating that the claim is open to refutation from the people of the Sunnah. He then analyzes the Mu'tazilite statement as a sentence with a subject and predicate: the predicate is 'externally adorned but internally corrupt', thus it is false. He provides two arguments: first, if the most beneficial were obligatory, then God would not have created the disbelieving poor person who suffers in both worlds, nor the one afflicted with illnesses, which contradicts observable reality. Second, if the most beneficial were obligatory, there would be no room for God to bestow favors preferentially, and God would not have choice in His actions, which contradicts the Quranic verses that affirm God's absolute will and choice. Then he clarifies the correct Sunni position: there is nothing obligatory upon God, because all His actions are permissible by essence, occurring either as beneficence or justice. Nothing is rationally obligatory or impossible regarding His actions.

Key Terms
الإيجاب
الأصلح
التفضيل
الجائز
العقل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that denying obligation on God means God acts arbitrarily without wisdom.
Correction: The passage actually affirms that God's actions are either beneficence (iḥsān) or justice (ʿadl), so they are not arbitrary; they are based on wisdom but not externally imposed.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what would be the consequence if the most beneficial (al-aṣlaḥ) were obligatory upon God?
A) God would not create any suffering.
B) God would have no room for preferential grace (tafḍīl).
C) God would be unjust.
D) Reason would become the judge of God's actions.

Key Takeaway
God is not obligated to do anything; His actions are exercises of His will, wisdom, and justice.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see someone suffering unjustly or living in poverty, do you ever feel that God should have done better for them? After reading that God is not obligated to do the most beneficial, what would you say to that feeling? Will you now surrender your sense of entitlement and trust His choice completely, even when it hurts?
?
The passage says God's actions are all either beneficence or justice. Think of a trial you are facing right now. Can you accept it as either an act of mercy (warning, expiation) or justice? What would change in your attitude if you truly believed God owes you nothing and yet gives you everything? Will you thank Him today for unearned favors?
